Checkpoint
According to the logician's convention (iṣṭilāḥ ahl al-manṭiq), what does the term 'essential' (dhātī) refer to?
A) Any term that indicates a necessary attribute of the thing
B) A term that indicates what is prior in existence to the thing's essence
C) A universal term that is predicated in answer to 'what is it?' (mā huwa)
D) A term that indicates a part of the thing's aggregate

Key Takeaway
In logic, 'essential' is technically defined as a universal term answering 'what is it?', resolving the puzzle that the quiddity term itself cannot be essential.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Given the three essential predicables (genus, species, differentia), identify which ones answer 'what is it?' and explain why 'animal' and 'rational' are considered essential for man but 'man' itself is not essential in the logical sense.
?
Write a brief explanation of the shift in meaning from the linguistic 'essential' to the logical 'essential', using the example of 'human' as a species.

What Answers 'What Is It?' – Conformity and Implication
Classification of expressions answering 'what is it?'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which expressions correctly answer 'what is it?' and distinguish between the two modes of indication: conformity and implication.

Core Idea
A single term like 'human' answers 'what is it?' by implying all essentials, not just by its name.

When you are asked 'what is a human?', you might say 'human' or 'rational animal'. Which one actually tells you the essence? In this lesson, we explore how expressions indicate quiddity – either by directly matching the full meaning (conformity) or by containing the essential parts (implication). Understanding this will help you see why a simple term can be a valid answer and how a definition works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Question
The question 'what is it?' (mā huwa) asks for the essence or reality of a thing. In logic, the answer must be an expression that indicates that essence.
2
Distinguish the Two Modes of Indication
An expression indicates its meaning either by conformity (muṭābaqa) – its whole meaning corresponds to the word – or by implication (taḍamman) – it includes the essential parts as part of its meaning. For example, 'human' by conformity means the entire human; by implication it means 'animal' and 'rational'.
Implication is like a container: a word implies its essential parts even if not stated separately.
3
Analyze the Simple Term Answer
If asked 'what is human?', answering simply 'human' is valid. The word 'human' indicates the full essence by conformity (it means exactly human) and implies all essentials (animal, rational) by implication. So a single term can answer the essence question.
This shows that definitions are not the only valid answers; simple terms work due to implication.
4
Analyze the Compound Answer
A compound answer like 'rational animal' also works. Here 'animal' and 'rational' each individually indicate their own meanings by conformity, and together they imply the entire human essence. This is the classic definition (ḥadd).
The compound answer is more explicit, but the core logic is the same.
5
Consider a Descriptive Answer
The author notes that even a longer description like 'a substance with three dimensions, breathing, sensitive, moving by will, rational' is a correct answer. This includes accidental attributes, but it still identifies the essence because it includes the essential differentia 'rational'.
This is a rasm (description) rather than a ḥadd (real definition), but it still answers 'what is it?' correctly because it uniquely identifies the thing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۸۱۰۲] فصل : [ في الدال وغير الدال ]
ولما كان الذاتي ينقسم إلى الدال على الماهية وإلى غير الدال؛ فالتعرض للدال على الماهية من اللوازم، وذلك هو الذي يجاب به حين يسأل عن الشيء أنه ما هو أي ما ذاته وحقيقته. والصالح لهذا الجواب هو اللفظ المطابق لمعناه المتضمن لجميع ذاتياته أو المقول الدال عليه. فإذا سئل عن الإنسان مثلا أنه «ما هو ؟ فيقال: إنه إنسان». والإنسان لفظ مفرد دال على تمام معناه بالمطابقة، وعلى جميع ذاتياته بالتضمن ولو قلت: «إنه حيوان ناطق» فهذا قول يدل على تمام معنى الحيوان والناطق بالمطابقة على جميع ذاتيات هذا، وذلك بالتضمن فيدل على حقيقة الإنسان كذلك. ولو قلت في الجواب: «إنه جوهر ذو أبعاد ثلاثة متنفس / حساس متحرك بالإرادة ناطق» وقد أجبت على وجه الصواب أيضًا.
Section: [ On what indicates and what does not indicate ]
Since the essential is divided into what indicates the quiddity and what does not indicate, then attention to what indicates the quiddity is among the necessary things, and that is what is answered when one asks about a thing 'what is it?', i.e., what is its essence and reality. And that which is suitable for this answer is the expression that corresponds to its meaning, encompassing all its essentials, or the speech indicating it. So if one asks about 'human', for example, 'what is it?', one says: 'It is a human.' And 'human' is a single term that indicates its full meaning by conformity, and all its essentials by implication. And if you say: 'It is a rational animal,' this is speech that indicates the full meaning of 'animal' and 'rational' by conformity, and all the essentials of this by implication, so it indicates the reality of 'human' likewise. And if you say in the answer: 'It is a substance possessing three dimensions, breathing, sensitive, moving by will, rational,' you have answered correctly as well.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a classification and explanation of the type of expression that answers the question 'what is it?' (mā huwa). The author begins by noting that the essential (dhātī) is divided into what indicates the quiddity (al-dāl 'alā al-māhiyya) and what does not. The focus here is on the former, which is used in response to the question about the essence or reality of a thing. The suitable answer is an expression that either: (1) is a single term that corresponds to its meaning exactly (muṭābiq) and implies all its essentials (taḍamman), such as the word 'human' when asked 'what is it?'—it indicates the full meaning of human by conformity and all its essentials (like animality and rationality) by implication; or (2) is a phrase or speech (qawl) that indicates the full meaning of each part by conformity and all essentials by implication, like saying 'rational animal'—here 'animal' and 'rational' each indicate their own meanings by conformity, and together they imply the essentials of human. The author also mentions a more detailed definition adding accidental attributes ('possessing three dimensions, breathing, sensitive, moving by will, rational') which still correctly indicates the essence, though it includes accidents. This shows that a definition can include accidental attributes (a description, rasm) as long as it sufficiently identifies the essence. The passage establishes the logical basis for definition (ḥadd) and description (rasm) as answers to 'what is it?'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does the word 'human' (insān) indicate the essence when answering 'what is it?'?
A) By conformity alone, since it is a single term.
B) By implication only, since it is not a definition.
C) By both conformity (its full meaning) and implication (all essentials).
D) It does not indicate the essence; only a compound expression does.

Key Takeaway
An expression answers 'what is it?' by indicating the essence either through conformity to its full meaning or implication of all essentials; both single terms and compound definitions are valid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Take the term 'zakāh' (alms tax). Construct an answer to 'what is zakāh?' using a single term (e.g., 'zakāh') and explain how it indicates the essence by conformity and implication. Then construct a compound answer (e.g., 'zakāh is a specific portion of wealth given to the poor') and analyze its indication modes.
?
Task 2: The definition of 'bay' (sale) in Hanafi fiqh is 'the exchange of property for property by mutual consent'. Identify which parts of this definition indicate by conformity and which by implication. Does this definition answer 'what is it?' correctly according to the criteria in the passage?
